–ó–∞–¥–æ—Ä–Ω–æ–≤–∞ –Ω–µ —Ö–≤–∞—Ç–∞–µ—Çüò¢üò¢üò¢, —Ç–æ–∂–µ –º–æ–≥ –±—ã –∞–Ω–∞–ª–∏–∑–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å –ø—Ä–æ–∏—Å—Ö–æ–¥—è—â–µ–µ –≤ –º–∏—Ä–µ, –∫–∞–∫–æ–π –≥—Ä–∞–º–æ—Ç–Ω—ã–π –±—ã–ª —á–µ–ª–æ–≤–µ–∫üò¢üò¢üò¢
My dear Russian readers, allow me to share my reflections on the unfolding events in North America since the ascension of President Donald Trump to power. For those seeking to grasp the intricacies of American affairs, I recommend my previous articles, which I write nearly daily in both English and Russian.        Today, I shall address the tariff war unleashed by the U.S. administration. Regardless of how we, the residents of North America, view Trump, his actions‚Äîshocking to the liberal swamp‚Äîdemonstrate that he has gone all in. There appears to be no alternative path to reform: either ignite a full-scale war or subject one‚Äôs opponents to an economic cold shower. In this brief note, I cannot unravel the full complexity of geopolitical maneuvers at play, but I shall highlight the key points.         The apparent chaos surrounding tariffs against Canada and Mexico is, in reality, laden with profound political implications. The entrenched liberal elites of Canada and Mexico, otherwise resistant to change, now find themselves under immense pressure. In Canada, the Conservative Party, led by Pierre Poilievre, has been nipping at the heels of Justin Trudeau‚Äôs Liberals for over a year, demanding change in the wake of the COVID-19 crisis. Yet the liberal establishment, loyal to the British Crown, refuses to yield. On the eve of Trump‚Äôs inauguration, they effectively sidelined the Canadian Parliament, placing it in "prorogation" to reorganize their leadership and cling to power at any cost.         But what is that cost? Mark Carney‚Äîa banker-oligarch, a freeman of the City of London, and former Governor of the Bank of England‚Äîis one of the key figures behind this process. Beneath the surface of the iceberg, a far more profound struggle unfolds: a contest between the Republic of the United States and the British Crown. Yes, they are allies, but they do not wish to split the spoils evenly. And Canada? It is a vast land, rich in resources rivaling those of Russia‚Äîa coveted slice of the global pie, now fiercely contested by the world‚Äôs power brokers.         The outcome of this struggle will be a reconfiguration of U.S.-Canada relations, a transformation of Canada‚Äôs political architecture, and, perhaps, the country‚Äôs eventual integration into a North American Union as the 51st state of the United States. Should this come to pass, the world will witness the emergence of a "Super-America", eclipsing even the Soviet Union in scale. This would fundamentally alter the global balance of power, enabling the United States to preserve its hegemonic imperial standing. For Washington, there is simply no other viable strategy to counter the forces shaping the New World Order.         Already today, February 2, Conservative leader Pierre Poilievre has issued a call to the nation: to make Canada great, to preserve its sovereignty, and to abolish internal tariffs between Provinces that stifle economic growth. Yet Canadians should not reach for the popcorn just yet‚Äîthe tariff war heralds not a spectacle, but a recession of immense magnitude, and perhaps even the disintegration of the country itself.
